**GT:** `-0.661172493025524*v - 1.16984597672115*x**3 - 0.330586246512762*log(Abs(v) + 1)`

Let me analyze the key components:
1. A term proportional to `v`
2. A term proportional to `x**3`
3. A term proportional to `log(Abs(v) + 1)`

The `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term is crucial - it's a nonlinear function of `|v|` that cannot be replicated by polynomials, exponentials in x, or piecewise linear functions.

Let me check which candidates have basis functions that could produce `log(Abs(v) + 1)`:

**Key analysis:** `log(Abs(v) + 1)` is a smooth, concave function of `|v|`. It cannot be exactly represented by:
- `v*Abs(v)` (quadratic-like)
- `Max(0, v)` and `Max(0, -v)` (piecewise linear, sum = `Abs(v)`)
- `v**3` (cubic)
- `(Abs(v) + 1)**3` (cubic in |v|)
- `Abs(v)` (piecewise linear)
- `v*exp(c*Abs(v))` 
- `exp(c*Abs(v))*Max(0, v)` type terms
- `v/(Abs(v)+1)` (rational)
- Polynomials in v

None of these basis functions can exactly reproduce `log(Abs(v) + 1)`. The logarithm is transcendental and linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, rational, and piecewise linear functions.

Let me check every candidate systematically:

- **Candidates 1-9, 11, 15-33, 35, 37-50**: Use combinations of `Max(0,v)`, `Max(0,-v)`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, `(Abs(v)+1)**3`, `Abs(v)`, `v/(Abs(v)+1)`, polynomials, exponentials in x, `tanh`, `sin` — none contain `log(Abs(v)+1)` or any logarithmic function of v.

- **Candidate 14**: Rational functions of `Abs(v)` — cannot produce log.

- **Candidate 16**: `c8*v*log(c9*Abs(x) + 1)` — this is log in x, not in v. Cannot match `log(Abs(v)+1)`.

- **Candidate 25**: Has `v*exp(c7*Abs(v))` — exponential, not log.

- **Candidate 34**: Has `v*sin(c7*log(c8*x**2+1)+c9)` — log of x, not v.

- **Candidate 36**: `c5*v*exp(c6*x)` — no log of v.

- **Candidate 42**: `c4*v*exp(c5*Abs(v))` — exponential in |v|, not log.

None of the candidates contain a `log(Abs(v) + c)` term or any logarithmic function of v. Since `log(Abs(v) + 1)` is linearly independent from all the basis functions present in every candidate, no candidate can exactly match the GT.
